<p>World literacy is lower for females than for males. The CIA World Factbook presents an estimate from 2010 which shows that 80% of women are literate, compared to 88.6% of men (aged 15 and over). Literacy rates are lowest in South and West Asia, and in parts of Sub-Saharan Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Women_in_politics">Women in politics</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sirimavo_Bandaranaike_1961_(cropped)_5.PNG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="294" data-file-width="216" decoding="async" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Sirimavo_Bandaranaike_1961_%28cropped%29_5.PNG/150px-Sirimavo_Bandaranaike_1961_%28cropped%29_5.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/Sirimavo_Bandaranaike_1961_%28cropped%29_5.PNG 1.5x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sirimavo_Bandaranaike_1961_(cropped)_5.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sirimavo_Bandaranaike" title="Sirimavo Bandaranaike">Sirimavo Bandaranaike</a> was the first female <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>; she was democratically elected in <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> in 1960.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_women%27s_suffrage" title="Timeline of women's suffrage">Timeline of women's suffrage</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_elected_and_appointed_female_heads_of_state_and_government" title="List of elected and appointed female heads of state and government">List of elected and appointed female heads of state and government</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg"><img alt="A world map showing female governmental participation by country, 2010." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1502" data-file-width="2402" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg/310px-Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg/465px-Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg/620px-Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map3.8Government_Participation_by_Women_compressed.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A world map showing female governmental participation by country, 2010.</div></div></div>
<p>Women are underrepresented in government in most countries. In January 2019, the global average of women in national assemblies was 24.3%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">Suffrage</a> is the civil right to vote, and <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage" title="Women's suffrage">women's suffrage</a> movements have a long <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_women%27s_suffrage" title="Timeline of women's suffrage">historic timeline</a>. For example, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage_in_the_United_States" title="Women's suffrage in the United States">women's suffrage in the United States</a> was achieved gradually, first at state and local levels in the late 19th and early 20th centuries, then in 1920 when women in the US received universal suffrage with the passage of the <a href="/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution">Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution</a>. Some Western countries were slow to allow women to vote, notably Switzerland, where women gained the right to vote in federal elections in 1971, and in the canton of <a href="/wiki/Appenzell_Innerrhoden" title="Appenzell Innerrhoden">Appenzell Innerrhoden</a> women were granted the right to vote on local issues only in 1991, when the canton was forced to do so by the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Supreme_Court_of_Switzerland" title="Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland">Federal Supreme Court of Switzerland</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a>, in 1984, through <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_women%27s_suffrage_referendum,_1984" title="Liechtenstein women's suffrage referendum, 1984">a women's suffrage referendum</a>.
</p>
<h2><span id="Science.2C_literature_and_art"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Science,_literature_and_art">Science, literature and art</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_science" title="Women in science">Women in science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Women_artists" title="Women artists">Women artists</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Women_writers" title="Women writers">Women writers</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_(Pastell_1878).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="517" data-file-width="361" decoding="async" height="243" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg/170px-Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg/255px-Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg/340px-Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_%28Pastell_1878%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Franz_von_Lenbach_-_Clara_Schumann_(Pastell_1878).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>German composer <a href="/wiki/Clara_Schumann" title="Clara Schumann">Clara Schumann</a> in 1878</div></div></div>
<p>Women have, throughout history, made contributions to science, <a href="/wiki/Literature" title="Literature">literature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Art" title="Art">art</a>. One area where women have been permitted most access historically was that of <a href="/wiki/Obstetrics" title="Obstetrics">obstetrics</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gynecology" title="Gynecology">gynecology</a> (prior to the 18th century, caring for pregnant women in Europe was undertaken by women; from the mid 18th century onwards, medical monitoring of pregnant women started to require rigorous formal education, to which women did not generally have access, and thus the practice was largely transferred to men).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gelis_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gelis-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Writing was generally also considered acceptable for upper-class women, although achieving success as a female writer in a male-dominated world could be very difficult; as a result of several women writers adopted a male pen name (e.g. <a href="/wiki/George_Sand" title="George Sand">George Sand</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Eliot" title="George Eliot">George Eliot</a>).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>
Women have been <a href="/wiki/Composer" title="Composer">composers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musician" title="Musician">instrumental performers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Singer" title="Singer">singers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Conducting" title="Conducting">conductors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musicology" title="Musicology">music scholars</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_teacher" title="Music teacher">music educators</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_criticism" title="Music criticism">music critics</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_journalist" title="Music journalist">music journalists</a> and other musical professions. There are music movements,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2018)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> events and genres related to women, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's issues</a> and <a href="/wiki/Feminism" title="Feminism">feminism</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the 2010s, while women comprise a significant proportion of <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classical_music" title="Classical music">classical music</a> singers, and a significant proportion of songwriters (many of them being singer-songwriters), there are few women <a href="/wiki/Record_producer" title="Record producer">record producers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_journalist" title="Music journalist">rock critics</a> and rock instrumentalists. Although there have been a huge number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_women_composers" title="List of women composers">women composers</a> in classical music, from the Medieval period to the present day, women composers are significantly underrepresented in the <a href="/wiki/Western_canon" title="Western canon">commonly performed classical music repertoire</a>, music history textbooks and music encyclopedias; for example, in the <i>Concise Oxford History of Music</i>, <a href="/wiki/Clara_Schumann" title="Clara Schumann">Clara Schumann</a> is one of the only female composers who is mentioned.</p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marie_Curie_1903.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="280" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Marie_Curie_1903.jpg/150px-Marie_Curie_1903.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Marie_Curie_1903.jpg/225px-Marie_Curie_1903.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/93/Marie_Curie_1903.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marie_Curie_1903.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Marie Curie</a> was the first woman to be awarded a <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">Nobel Prize</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Women comprise a significant proportion of instrumental soloists in classical music and the percentage of women in orchestras is increasing. A 2015 article on concerto soloists in major Canadian orchestras, however, indicated that 84% of the soloists with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orchestre_Symphonique_de_Montreal" title="Orchestre Symphonique de Montreal">Orchestre Symphonique de Montreal</a> were men. In 2012, women still made up just 6% of the top-ranked <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Philharmonic" title="Vienna Philharmonic">Vienna Philharmonic</a> orchestra. Women are less common as instrumental players in popular music genres such as rock and <a href="/wiki/Heavy_metal_music" title="Heavy metal music">heavy metal</a>, although there have been a number of notable female instrumentalists and <a href="/wiki/All-female_band" title="All-female band">all-female bands</a>. Women are particularly underrepresented in <a href="/wiki/Extreme_metal" title="Extreme metal">extreme metal</a> genres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Women are also underrepresented in orchestral conducting, music criticism/music journalism, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_producer" title="Music producer">music producing</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sound_engineering" title="Sound engineering">sound engineering</a>. While women were discouraged from composing in the 19th century, and there are few women <a href="/wiki/Musicology" title="Musicology">musicologists</a>, women became involved in <a href="/wiki/Music_education" title="Music education">music education</a> "... to such a degree that women dominated [this field] during the later half of the 19th century and well into the 20th century."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parlorsongs.com_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-parlorsongs.com-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to Jessica Duchen, a music writer for London's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, women musicians in classical music are "... too often judged for their appearances, rather than their talent" and they face pressure "... to look sexy onstage and in photos."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music.cbc.ca_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-music.cbc.ca-124">[124]</a></sup> Duchen states that while "[t]here are women musicians who refuse to play on their looks, ... the ones who do tend to be more materially successful."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-music.cbc.ca_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-music.cbc.ca-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the UK's Radio 3 editor, Edwina Wolstencroft, the classical music industry has long been open to having women in performance or entertainment roles, but women are much less likely to have positions of authority, such as being the <a href="/wiki/Conducting" title="Conducting">leader of an orchestra</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-125">[125]</a></sup> In popular music, while there are many women singers recording songs, there are very few women behind the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audio_mixer" title="Audio mixer">audio console</a> acting as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_producer" title="Music producer">music producers</a>, the individuals who direct and manage the recording process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg"><img alt="An oil painting of a young woman dressed in a flowing, white dress sitting on a chair with a red drape. An easel rests on her knees and she is evidently drawing. She is gazing directly at the observer." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5921" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg/200px-Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg/300px-Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg/400px-Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Villers_Young_Woman_Drawing.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Portrait_of_Charlotte_du_Val_d%27Ognes_(Marie-Denise_Villers)" title="Portrait of Charlotte du Val d'Ognes (Marie-Denise Villers)">Portrait of Charlotte du Val d'Ognes</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Marie-Denise_Villers" title="Marie-Denise Villers">Marie-Denise Villers</a> (1801), depicts a feminine spirit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGreer2001142_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGreer2001142-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJames1997xiv_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJames1997xiv-128">[128]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_symbol">Gender symbol</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gender_symbol" title="Gender symbol">Gender symbol</a></div>
<p>The glyph (♀) for the <a href="/wiki/Venus" title="Venus">planet</a> and Roman goddess <a href="/wiki/Venus_(mythology)" title="Venus (mythology)">Venus</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Aphrodite" title="Aphrodite">Aphrodite</a> in Greek, is the <a href="/wiki/Gender_symbol" title="Gender symbol">symbol</a> used in biology for the female sex.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Stearn1962_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Stearn1962-130">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schott2005_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Schott2005-131">[131]</a></sup> In ancient alchemy, the Venus symbol stood for <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> and was associated with <a href="/wiki/Femininity" title="Femininity">femininity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schott2005_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-Schott2005-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Femininity">Femininity</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Femininity" title="Femininity">Femininity</a></div>
<p><i>Femininity</i> (also called <i>womanliness</i> or <i>girlishness</i>) is a set of attributes, behaviors, and roles generally associated with women and girls. Although femininity is socially constructed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-132">[132]</a></sup> some behaviors considered feminine are biologically influenced.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.com_132-1"><a href="#cite_note-books.google.com-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gender,_Nature,_and_Nurture_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gender,_Nature,_and_Nurture-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-135">[135]</a></sup> The extent to which femininity is biologically or socially influenced is subject to debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_134-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gender,_Nature,_and_Nurture_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gender,_Nature,_and_Nurture-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceC_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceC-135">[135]</a></sup> It is distinct from the definition of the biological female sex,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> as both males and females can exhibit feminine traits.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Used in Middle English from c. 1300, meaning 'a child of either sex, a young person'. Its derivation is uncertain, perhaps from an Old English word which has not survived: another theory is that it developed from Old English 'gyrela', meaning 'dress, apparel': or was a diminutive form of a borrowing from another West Germanic Language. (Middle Low German has Gör, Göre, meaning 'girl or small child'.) "girl, n.". OED Online. September 2013. Oxford University Press. 13 September 2013</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">By late 14th century a distinction was arising between female children, often called 'gay girls' – and male, or 'knave girls' -: a1375 William of Palerne (1867) l. 816 ' Whan þe gaye gerles were in-to þe gardin come, Faire floures þei founde.' ('When the gay girls came into the garden, Fair flowers they found.') By the 16th century, the unsupported word had begun to mean specifically a female: 1546 J. Heywood Dialogue Prouerbes Eng. Tongue i. x. sig. D, 'The boy thy husbande, and thou the gyrle his wyfe.' The usage meaning 'child of either sex' survived much longer in <a href="/wiki/Hiberno-English" title="Hiberno-English">Irish English</a>. "girl, n.". OED Online. September 2013. Oxford University Press. 13 September 2013</span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFInstitute_of_Medicine_(US)_Committee_on_Understanding_the_Biology_of_Sex_and_Gender_DifferencesWizemannPardue2001">Institute of Medicine (US) Committee on Understanding the Biology of Sex and Gender Differences; Wizemann, Theresa M.; Pardue, Mary-Lou (2 July 2001). <a class="external text" href="https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK222286/" rel="nofollow">"Sex Begins in the Womb"</a>. <i>Exploring the Biological Contributions to Human Health</i>. National Academies Press (US). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doi_(identifier)" title="Doi (identifier)">doi</a>:<a class="external text" href="https://doi.org/10.17226%2F10028" rel="nofollow">10.17226/10028</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-309-07281-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-309-07281-6"><bdi>978-0-309-07281-6</bdi></a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PMID_(identifier)" title="PMID (identifier)">PMID</a> <a class="external text" href="//pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/25057540" rel="nofollow">25057540</a>. <q>All human individuals—whether they have an XX, an XY, or an atypical sex chromosome combination—begin development from the same starting point. During early development the gonads of the fetus remain undifferentiated; that is, all fetal genitalia are the same and are phenotypically female. After approximately 6 to 7 weeks of gestation, however, the expression of a gene on the Y chromosome induces changes that result in the development of the testes.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Sex+Begins+in+the+Womb&amp;rft.btitle=Exploring+the+Biological+Contributions+to+Human+Health&amp;rft.pub=National+Academies+Press+%28US%29&amp;rft.date=2001-07-02&amp;rft_id=info%3Apmid%2F25057540&amp;rft_id=info%3Adoi%2F10.17226%2F10028&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-309-07281-6&amp;rft.au=Institute+of+Medicine+%28US%29+Committee+on+Understanding+the+Biology+of+Sex+and+Gender+Differences&amp;rft.au=Wizemann%2C+Theresa+M.&amp;rft.au=Pardue%2C+Mary-Lou&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov%2Fbooks%2FNBK222286%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation news cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/world-asia-21363894" rel="nofollow">"Woman burned alive for 'sorcery' in Papua New Guinea"</a>. <i>BBC News</i>. 7 February 2013.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=BBC+News&amp;rft.atitle=Woman+burned+alive+for+%27sorcery%27+in+Papua+New+Guinea&amp;rft.date=2013-02-07&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.bbc.co.uk%2Fnews%2Fworld-asia-21363894&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-69">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/news/saudi-arabia-beheading-sorcery-shocking-2011-12-12" rel="nofollow">"Saudi Arabia: Beheading for 'sorcery' shocking | Amnesty International"</a>. Amnesty.org<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2014-04-19</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Saudi+Arabia%3A+Beheading+for+%27sorcery%27+shocking+%26%23124%3B+Amnesty+International&amp;rft.pub=Amnesty.org&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amnesty.org%2Fen%2Fnews%2Fsaudi-arabia-beheading-sorcery-shocking-2011-12-12&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-70">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation news cs1"><a class="external text" href="http://edition.cnn.com/2011/12/13/world/meast/saudi-arabia-beheading/" rel="nofollow">"Saudi woman beheaded for 'witchcraft and sorcery'<span class="cs1-kern-right"></span>"</a>. <i>CNN.com</i>. 14 December 2011.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=CNN.com&amp;rft.atitle=Saudi+woman+beheaded+for+%27witchcraft+and+sorcery%27&amp;rft.date=2011-12-14&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fedition.cnn.com%2F2011%2F12%2F13%2Fworld%2Fmeast%2Fsaudi-arabia-beheading%2F&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-71">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In 2006, the UN Secretary-General's <i>In-depth study on all forms of violence against women</i> found that (p. 113): "Marital rape may be prosecuted in at least 104 States. Of these, 32 have made marital rape a specific criminal offence, while the remaining 74 do not exempt marital rape from general rape provisions. Marital rape is not a prosecutable offence in at least 53 States. Four States criminalize marital rape only when the spouses are judicially separated. Four States are considering legislation that would allow marital rape to be prosecuted."<a class="external autonumber" href="https://www.un.org/womenwatch/daw/vaw/publications/English%20Study.pdf" rel="nofollow">[1]</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-72">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a>, marital rape was made illegal in 1991. The views of Sir Matthew Hale, a 17th-century jurist, published in <i>The History of the Pleas of the Crown (1736)</i>, stated that a husband cannot be guilty of the rape of his wife because the wife "<i>hath given up herself in this kind to her husband, which she cannot retract</i>"; in England and Wales this would remain law for more than 250 years, until it was abolished by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Appellate_Committee_of_the_House_of_Lords" title="Appellate Committee of the House of Lords">Appellate Committee of the House of Lords</a>, <a class="external text" href="http://www.bailii.org/uk/cases/UKHL/1991/12.html" rel="nofollow">in the case of <i>R v R</i> in 1991.</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-73">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For example, in <a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a>, marriage regulations state that a wife must obey her husband and must not leave home without his permission.<a class="external autonumber" href="http://www2.ohchr.org/english/bodies/hrc/docs/ngos/Yemen%27s%20darkside-discrimination_Yemen_HRC101.pdf" rel="nofollow">[2]</a> In <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> husbands have a legal right to "punish" their wives. The criminal code states at Paragraph 41 that there is no crime if an act is committed while exercising a legal right; examples of legal rights include: "The punishment of a wife by her husband, the disciplining by parents and teachers of children under their authority within certain limits prescribed by law or by custom".<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20121021100954/http://law.case.edu/saddamtrial/documents/Iraqi_Penal_Code_1969.pdf" rel="nofollow">"The Penal Code – With Amendments"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>. Iraqi Ministry of Justice. Archived from <a class="external text" href="http://law.case.edu/saddamtrial/documents/Iraqi_Penal_Code_1969.pdf" rel="nofollow">the original</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span> on 2012-10-21<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2012-10-21</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=The+Penal+Code+%E2%80%93+With+Amendments&amp;rft.pub=Iraqi+Ministry+of+Justice&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Flaw.case.edu%2Fsaddamtrial%2Fdocuments%2FIraqi_Penal_Code_1969.pdf&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span> In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a> the Family Code states that the husband is the head of the household; the wife owes her obedience to her husband; a wife has to live with her husband wherever he chooses to live; and wives must have their husbands' authorization to bring a case in court or to initiate other legal proceedings.<a class="external autonumber" href="https://www.hrw.org/reports/2002/drc/Congo0602-09.htm" rel="nofollow">[3]</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-74">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation web cs1"><a class="external text" href="https://www.amnesty.org/en/news/colombian-authorities-fail-stop-or-punish-sexual-violence-against-women-2012-10-04" rel="nofollow">"Colombian authorities fail to stop or punish sexual violence against women | Amnesty International"</a>. Amnesty.org<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">2014-04-19</span></span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Colombian+authorities+fail+to+stop+or+punish+sexual+violence+against+women+%26%23124%3B+Amnesty+International&amp;rft.pub=Amnesty.org&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.amnesty.org%2Fen%2Fnews%2Fcolombian-authorities-fail-stop-or-punish-sexual-violence-against-women-2012-10-04&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AWoman"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-137"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-137">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Ferrante, Joan (January 2010). Sociology: A Global Perspective (7th ed.). Belmont, CA: Thomson Wadsworth. pp. 269–272. ISBN 978-0-8400-3204-1.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
